- **Pavement lead-in onto the first cleared taxiway (large gap only).** When a user taxiway sequence is given and the nearest node ON the first cleared taxiway is more than `TaxiLeadIn.TriggerMeters` (75 m) from the aircraft, `LoadRoute` starts the constrained route from the aircraft's nearest *in-component* graph node (`FindNearestNode(..., requiredComponentId: destComponentId)`) instead of pre-snapping onto the taxiway. This lets `TaxiRouter.FindConstrainedPath` build its pavement-following lead-in (the Step-1 `AStarSearch`) onto the taxiway — apron taxilanes — rather than beelining across the apron/grass (CYYZ GB/GC → A: a 297 m beeline + 180° pivot, "in the grass crossing AJ", 2026-06-17). The lead-in is **accepted only** when the router honoured the clearance (`ConstrainedFallbackReason == null`) AND its distance is within `gap × 2.5 + 300 m` (`TaxiLeadIn.IsAcceptable`, a dead-end guard); otherwise the route is rebuilt from the on-taxiway node (today's behaviour) and the summary is prepended with *"Could not compute a path onto taxiway X along the apron; route starts on X."* On success the summary names the lead-in: *"Route to Runway 23 via A, H. First taxi via 4 and AJ to reach A. …"* (`TaxiLeadIn.Clause`). The ≤ 75 m common case (gate on/near its taxiway) is byte-for-byte unchanged, and `TryRecalculateRoute`/unconstrained routes are untouched. Verified in-sim at CYYZ (GB/GC → runway 23 via A, H, 2026-06-17): the route starts at the apron node and the lead-in tracks the AJ taxiway centreline within ~3 m onto A, replacing the earlier ~64 m straight beeline across the grass. Do NOT remove the pre-snap for the common case — it is the LEPA anchoring fix; the lead-in only replaces it when the first taxiway is far.

Details: [docs/taxi-guidance.md](docs/taxi-guidance.md).

### GSX Gate Integration, Docking Guidance & Distance Units

**Feature (branch `feat/gsx-taxi-gate-integration`):** Three coupled subsystems layered on taxi guidance — (1) selecting a GSX parking position by driving its in-sim menu, (2) audio docking guidance to the stop position (VDGS/marshalling analog), and (3) an app-wide metres/feet distance toggle. Verified with console probes under `tools/`, not xUnit (run `dotnet run --project tools/<Name> -p:Platform=x64`): `DockingProbe`, `DistanceUnitsProbe`, `GsxProfileProbe` (`--all` sweep / `--audit` robustness), `GsxAirplaneProbe`.

**Domain boundary with PR #84 ("Fix GSX active service") — do not cross.** We own POSITIONING only: gate/stand selection, docking geometry, deice-pad positioning. PR #84 owns live SERVICE STATE (boarding/refuel/catering/deice/pushback status, timers, `GsxSettingsForm`). Don't add service-state logic here, and don't let docking read service vars.

**Key rules when touching this code:**

- **Gate-list source selection lives in `Services/GateDataSource.cs`.** GSX is authoritative when GSX is available (`CouatlStarted`) AND `GsxProfileLocator` finds a matching profile; otherwise navdata. `GsxNavdataMerger` overlays GSX metadata onto the navdata skeleton (navdata supplies positions GSX omits, matched by concourse+number). **Merger safety: no cross-concourse coordinate borrowing.** When a GSX gate HAS a concourse, a navdata candidate may only donate coordinates if its normalized concourse matches — otherwise the spot is DROPPED (routing a blind pilot to "A12" at B12's coordinates on another pier is worse than omission). **Spot position priority is `this_parking_pos` → navdata → stop position (LAST resort).** The GSX stop position is a VDGS NOSE-STOP reference, not an aircraft-datum location — using it as the spot position teleports the datum metres deep into the stand (sometimes at heading 0); docking is unaffected because it reads the preserved `StopLatitude/StopLongitude/StopHeading` fields directly. **GSX Python (`.py`) profiles are NOT parsed for the gate LIST** — only `.ini`. So large airports with a `.py` profile (e.g. EDDF `eddf-Aerosoft.py`) fall back to navdata for the LIST, even though the live GSX *menu* (used by the selector below) still works. Deice areas are GSX-only and excluded from the normal gate list (`GetDeiceAreas` is separate). **The DOCKING STOP, however, DOES consume `.py`** — see the per-aircraft stop-offset bullet below.
- **GSX `.py` per-aircraft stop offset applies to ALL non-deice gates (incl. `.ini`).** `TaxiAssistForm.ApplyGsxStopOffset` resolves GSX's per-aircraft longitudinal/lateral stop offset (metres) and feeds it to `DockingGuidanceManager.SetStopOffset` for every non-deice gate — `.ini` gates included. It previously SKIPPED the `.py` `customOffset` whenever the gate had a `StopLatitude` (i.e. `.ini` gates), wrongly assuming the `.ini` stop was already aircraft-exact. It isn't: the `.py` `customOffset` is GSX's PER-AIRCRAFT adjustment layered ON TOP of the static `.ini`/navdata base (same gate → different offset per airframe — EDDF A66: 777 = 5.3 m, A380 = 6.3 m, base = 1.65 m). Without this the 777 parked ~5.3 m short at every `.ini` airport (EDDF etc.). **Suffix changes the resolved function:** EDDF **A66** (no suffix) → 777 = **+5.3 m**; EDDF **A66A** (suffix "A") → 777 = **0 m** (that stand's function has no 777 table entry, so it correctly falls to base 0; an A320 there gets −2.5 m — proves it evaluates rather than parse-missing). Locked by `tools/GsxOffsetProbe` resolver-level asserts. A `STOPOFFSET` diagnostic line (icao / gate# / suffix / stopLatSet / ac / acId / resolved offset) is appended to `%APPDATA%\MSFSBlindAssist\logs\docking-aircraft.log` on each route-calculate for one-glance debugging of "offset is 0" reports. `GsxStopOffsetResolver` locates the airport `.py` (`GsxProfileLocator.TryFindPyProfile`, excludes `_handler.py`), parses it (`GsxPyProfileReader`, cached by path+last-write), and evaluates the gate's `customOffset` function (`GsxPyOffsetEvaluator`) for the resolved `GsxAircraftId`. **Aircraft resolution is UNIVERSAL** (`GsxAircraftIdMap.TryResolve(icao, wingspanMetres)`): idMajor/idMinor are DERIVED from the ICAO designator pattern (Boeing `B7Xd`→707+X·10, Airbus `A3YZ` narrowbody-literal/widebody-300+Y·10, Embraer literal) and ARC from wingspan (Annex-14 A&lt;15…F≥65 m); a thin exception table holds only irregulars (B787 bare-minor, A350 idMinor 1000, neo idMinor 1, A220, **and the 737 MAX family — `B37M`/`B38M`/`B39M`/`B3XM` → 737 family with closest-gauge minor**: the `B3xM` designators break the `B7Xd` pattern and used to resolve idMajor 0, silently losing every idMajor-keyed `.py` stop offset for one of the most common airliner families; locked by probe asserts). The raw ICAO is always kept so ICAO-keyed tables hit; idMajor 0 forces the base offset. Evaluator group fallback tries `"ARC-E"`, bare `"E"`, and `"Heavy"` (authors key differently; `"ARC-X"` dominates installed profiles). In `DockingGuidanceManager.UpdatePosition` the stop point is shifted (`ShiftStop`, equirectangular) BEFORE any distance is computed — longitudinal along `StopHeading`, lateral perpendicular (right=+). **`GsxOffset.Zero` is a strict no-op** (shift skipped) so behaviour is byte-identical to today; any miss at any layer (no profile/unknown aircraft/parse error) degrades to `Zero`. Logged as `stopOffL`/`stopOffLat` in `docking.log`. Measured golden: EDDF A66 / 777-300 = +5.3 m. Verified by `tools/GsxOffsetProbe` (golden + `--sweep` over all 72 profiles + a **universal installed-aircraft scan**: `AircraftCfgCatalog.EnumerateInstalled()` enumerates THIS machine's real fleet and asserts every distinct ICAO resolves without throwing — zero hardcoded expected values, so the probe works on any user's machine).
- **TITLE→ICAO catalog fallback (`Services/AircraftCfgCatalog.cs`).** The whole GSX/docking aircraft-resolution chain keys on the ICAO from SimConnect `ATC MODEL` (`SimConnectManager.ExtractIcaoFromAtcModel`). For the rare add-on whose ATC MODEL doesn't parse to a clean ICAO, `SimConnectManager` falls back to `AircraftCfgCatalog.TryGetIcaoByTitle(currentAircraftTitle)`. The catalog is a PURE, dependency-light service (file IO only — no WinForms/SimConnect/EFBModPackageManager deps, so the probe links it) that scans installed `aircraft.cfg` files under `<InstalledPackagesPath>\{Community,Official\OneStore,Official\Steam}\…\SimObjects\Airplanes` (depth-bounded so it never crawls texture trees), parsing each cfg's package-level `icao_type_designator` and every `[FLTSIM.N] title` into a `titleLower→icaoUpper` map. It resolves the packages root itself by reading `InstalledPackagesPath` from the FS2024/FS2020 `UserCfg.opt` locations. **Background + lazy + cached + thread-safe; NEVER throws** (any missing dir / locked file / malformed cfg degrades to empty/no-hit). The fallback runs ONLY when `ExtractIcaoFromAtcModel` returns empty, NEVER blocks the SimConnect callback (the scan/lookup is on a `Task.Run`), validates the result looks like an ICAO (2–4 alphanumerics), and — mirroring the door-offset background re-fire — sets `CurrentAircraftIcaoType` + re-fires `AircraftIcaoTypeDetected` when it later resolves. The common case (ATC model present) is byte-for-byte unchanged. The catalog is warmed via `BeginBuild()` at `Connect()` time so the fallback has near-zero latency.
- **`Services/Gsx/GsxGateSelector.cs` drives the live GSX menu via L-vars** (NOT the parsed profile) to select a stand: a bounded, backtracking, **page-aware DFS** (`TraverseAsync`). `ChooseAsync` is only ever called while the live menu is displaying the page containing the entry (choice values are page-relative — no pre-collection). Confirms via `SetGate_*` L-vars, which **lag** — they're polled up to ~6 s (`PollSetGateMatchAsync`), and when changing gates briefly hold the OLD gate. **Every run appends a full walk-log to `%APPDATA%\MSFSBlindAssist\logs\gsx-gate-select.log` — READ THIS FIRST when debugging a "gate not found".** Never choose a `ForbiddenAction` (WARP/Follow-Me/reposition/towing); only choose a positively-identified `SafeServicingAction`. **Leaf matching has a letterless-leaf bare-number fallback**: a GSX menu leaf with no concourse letter ("Parking 209") matches a navdata-lettered target ("P 209" — letter borrowed by the merger for display) on bare number alone; exact identity match is always tried first and the fallback is logged as `MATCH-BARENUMBER` (fixes guaranteed "not found" at EGLL-style airports). **`SelectGateAsync` has an `Interlocked` reentrancy latch** — two Calculate clicks could interleave two DFS traversals on one live GSX menu (the `IsMenuActive` guard reads false during every menu transition, so it cannot prevent this), pressing arbitrary wrong entries; the latch makes the second call return failure immediately.
- **`Services/Gsx/GsxMenuClassifier.cs` is the ONE tunable surface** (pure/stateless; all pattern arrays at the top). Two disambiguations are safety-critical and were each fixed against live menus:
  - **`IsBackUp = IsBack && !IsNext`** (mirror of `IsNextForward`). The back-patterns match "previous"/"◀", which also appear in the pagination entry "◀Previous Page". `BackOutAsync` MUST use `IsBackUp` (the true "↑ Back"), or backing out of a multi-page submenu presses "Previous Page" and the search gets stuck in that submenu (CONFIRMED EDDF). **The "main"/"top" back-patterns are full phrases ("main menu" / "back to top"), not bare words** — bare "main"/"top" false-positived on apron/terminal names like "Main Apron", classifying a drillable category as Back.
  - **Leaf-vs-Category order:** a parking COUNT suffix (`"(N suitable parkings)"`, via `CategoryCountRegex`) is the DEFINITIVE group-header signal → Category. **The count-suffix Category check runs FIRST — before `IsBack` and before leaf matching.** A `"(N suitable parkings)"` group like "Main Apron (12 suitable parkings)" classified as Back made every stand inside unreachable AND desynced `BackOutAsync`; and checking it before leaf matching keeps `"Apron A (8 suitable parkings)"` from being parsed as gate "8". THEN a concrete stand ID → `GateLeaf`, **even when the text contains a structural keyword** like "cargo"/"ramp"/"remote" (so `"Stand F211 … Ramp Cargo"` is a leaf, not a drillable category — CONFIRMED EDDF). THEN structural-keyword-only → Category. Do not reorder.
  - Identity matching: `NormalizeTargetIdentity` / `LooksLikeGate` reduce to concourse+number+suffix (e.g. "F222") and strip a leading 'G' from all-letter navdata names ("GF" → "F").
- **Docking (`Services/DockingGuidanceManager.cs` + `DockingGeometry.cs` + `ProximityBeeper.cs`)** is a standalone state machine (Idle→Armed→Docking→Stopped) fed from the SAME ~30 Hz position handler as taxi guidance but **independent of `TaxiGuidanceManager`**. It owns its OWN `TaxiSteeringTone` instance (lateral cue) + a `ProximityBeeper` (accelerating beep) + spoken metric milestones. To avoid two panning tones, `MainForm` calls `taxiGuidanceManager.SetSteeringToneSuppressed(dockingManager.IsActive)` each frame so only one sounds.
  - `DockingGeometry` is pure static + probe-tested. `alongM` = forward distance to stop, **datum-aligned**: the aircraft DATUM stops at the parking/stop position — an MSFS parking position (and a GSX stop position) is where the aircraft *reference* sits when correctly parked, and the scenery jetway is placed to reach the door for that datum location. **The per-aircraft `gsx.cfg` longitudinal door offset is NOT subtracted from the stop math, and the `SetDoorOffsetMetres` plumbing is removed end-to-end — do NOT reintroduce it.** It describes where the door is ON the airframe, not a stop offset; subtracting it parked a B777 ~26 m short (it had been telemetry-only dead plumbing since that fix). Only the door SIDE cue survives from `gsx.cfg` (see the `GsxAirplaneProfile` bullet). Per-airframe stop depth is the `.py` stop offset's job (`SetStopOffset`), which deice areas keep at `GsxOffset.Zero` (datum-aligned pad). The lateral cue is the **heading-error angle (`hdgErr`)**, NOT `CalculateCrossTrackError` (which assumes the aircraft is ahead of the reference and yields ±180° garbage when docking from behind).
  - **GSX static occupancy clamp (`DockingGeometry.ClampStopToOccupancy`, called in `UpdatePosition` right after `ShiftStop`).** GSX registers an aircraft as PARKED (offers arrival services + operates the jetway) only when its DATUM is inside a circle of radius ≈ the gate's `gatedistancethreshold` centred on `this_parking_pos` (= `_gate.Latitude/Longitude` for GSX gates) — **live-verified at KBOS E13 2026-06-13**: services at ≤25 m incl. 10 m BEHIND the point, reposition past it (so it is a RADIUS, not a forward-only segment; side / `radius{left,right}` do NOT govern static occupancy). The `.py` per-aircraft `SetStopOffset` can push the datum OUTSIDE that circle (KBOS E13 B772: offset → datum 31.5 m > 25 m circle → GSX offered "reposition" after a clean dock — the reported bug). The clamp pulls the post-offset stop back along the gate heading to `gatedistancethreshold − OccupancyClampMarginMetres (2 m)` (FLOORED AT 0 — a malformed profile with `gatedistancethreshold < 2 m` would otherwise pull the datum BEHIND `this_parking_pos`; real thresholds are 15–30 m so this never affects a legitimate gate, probe-locked by the `tiny-threshold` case) **only when** the base stop is itself inside the circle AND the shifted datum would land outside it; it is a **strict NO-OP** for deice pads, navdata-only gates (no `StopLatitude`/threshold), datums already inside the circle, and **VDGS-reliant gates whose stop sits BEYOND the threshold** (EDDF A66: stop 25.1 m, threshold 15 m — those are accepted ONLY via GSX's dynamic VDGS approach-dock, which a static placement even at the exact `.py` target does NOT trigger; clamping them would pull the datum far short of the bar and break jetway reach + the VDGS dock). `ClampBaseStopToleranceMetres (1 m)` keeps the author-set-`gatedistancethreshold == stop-distance` knife-edge (KBOS: both 25) on the CLAMP side despite float/coordinate noise. A one-shot `OCCUPANCY-CLAMP` line goes to `docking-aircraft.log` (latched by `_occupancyClampLogged`, reset per gate in `ResetLocked` — never per-frame IO). Probe-locked (`tools/DockingProbe`: KBOS fires→23 m, EDDF/KATL/inside-circle no-op); a scan of installed GSX profiles found ~850 gates in the affected band across essentially every major airport, so this was a widespread silent failure. Live-verified end-to-end: KBOS E13 (B772 → fixed), EIDW C406 (B738, base stop outside circle → fixed), EIDW C402 (B738, no-op), EDDF A66 (B77W, golden untouched). **Do NOT remove**, do not "simplify" it to clamp on `gatedistancethreshold` unconditionally (breaks EDDF-type gates), and clamp only the `.py`-shifted stop (never the navdata base point).
  - The docking lateral tone uses the **runway-lineup precision profile** (`UpdateHeadingErrorWithThresholds`, 0.5°/1.0°/15°), NOT the width-scaled `UpdateHeadingError` overload (whose `MIN_SCALE` clamp bottoms out at ~1.95°/3.9° — far too loose for parking).
  - `Services/Gsx/GsxAirplaneProfile.cs` reads each aircraft's `gsx.cfg` `[exit<preferredexit>] pos` (col1 = lateral, neg=left), matched by ICAO extracted from SimConnect `ATC MODEL` — **its ONLY consumer cue is the door SIDE** ("Jetway/Door on your left/right" at docking engage); the longitudinal column no longer feeds anything (see the datum-aligned bullet above). The ICAO map is built in the background and refreshed on aircraft change; the build is **single-flight via `Lazy`** (two concurrent multi-second scans no longer race), the `gsx.cfg` scan is **depth-bounded (6)** so texture/sound trees are never crawled, and `UserCfg.opt` parsing **excludes `InstalledPackagesPathNextBoot` lines** (which could resolve a not-yet-active packages path after a relocation). `MainForm.OnAircraftIcaoTypeDetected` locks `_refreshedIcaos` (concurrent `Task.Run` mutations of a plain HashSet) and rechecks the ICAO is still current before publishing the door side, so a late Refresh for the OLD aircraft can't clobber the NEW one.
- **Docking completion stops taxi guidance.** `DockingGuidanceManager` raises a `DockingCompleted` event once on the Docking→Stopped transition (including overshoot), fired OUTSIDE its lock. `MainForm` subscribes and calls `taxiGuidanceManager.StopGuidance()` (thread-safe + silent) so the flow ends cleanly instead of taxi sitting in LiningUp forever after parking.
- **Arrival ownership is ENGAGE-LATCHED, not gate-set.** `MainForm` feeds `taxiGuidanceManager.SetDockingActive(dockingGuidanceManager.IsActive)` — `IsActive` = the docking state machine is in Docking or Stopped, exposed as a **lock-free volatile snapshot** (one fewer docking-lock + zero SettingsManager static-lock reads per 30 Hz frame). Taxi speaks its FULL arrival sequence — parking countdown, "Stop. Hold position.", "Align with X", "Destination reached", "Parking brake." — right up until docking actually engages; once engaged, docking owns the rest of the arrival through Stopped and taxi stays quiet. **Do NOT widen this back to gate-set semantics** (the old `OwnsArrival` = gate set + docking enabled): a navdata gate where docking never engages (approach outside the 70° cone, stop beyond engage range, approximate navdata heading) then arrives in TOTAL verbal silence. The deliberate trade: a brief sequential overlap is possible (taxi's stop callout fires, then docking engages with its own countdown) — that's self-correcting and far better than silent arrivals. The same `IsActive` read also drives the steering-tone mute via `SetSteeringToneSuppressed`. **PENDING-aware wording (third state between "not engaged" and "engaged"):** `DockingGuidanceManager.IsArmedAwaitingEngage` (volatile snapshot, set per-frame in the Idle/Armed branch when detail math is available, the stop resolves >3 m ahead, and engage conditions aren't met; cleared on engage/reset/dispose) feeds `taxiGuidanceManager.SetDockingPending`. While pending, taxi's arrival wording REDIRECTS FORWARD — align announce gains "Then continue ahead for docking guidance.", aligned-enter says "Continue ahead. Docking guidance will take over." (NOT "Parking brake."), the 10 ft countdown directive and stopped-in-zone cue say continue instead of "Stop. Hold position.", and the LiningUp status readout says continue. Why: the GSX stop is routinely tens of metres past the navdata point where taxi's route ends, and a gate's GSX `gatedistancethreshold` can shrink the engage range BELOW that gap — KATL F3 2026-06-11: pilot was told "Parking brake." at the navdata point and sat 26 s at 33.7 m with docking Armed (engage range ~24 m from the gate's threshold), until they crept forward on their own. Announcements only — engage logic, tone ownership, and the engage-latch trade above are unchanged; a pending gate where docking never engages still gets the full (redirected) verbal arrival.
- **Jetway-precise lateral lineup (`DockingGuidanceManager.ComputeLineupError`).** Intercept dead-band tightened **8 ft → 1 ft** (the 8 ft band stopped correcting cross-track below 8 ft, parking up to ~2.4 m off centerline); `SaturationFt` 60 → 40 (a small residual still yields a usable correction angle). Cross-track convergence is a function of DISTANCE travelled, not time (`d(cross)/d(forward) = −sin(angle)`), so it closes the same per metre at 1 kt as at 5 kt — no slow-speed special-casing — and the continuous sqrt ramp never springs a late turn.
- **Final alignment turn completes earlier.** The intercept-fade squares the heading to pure gate heading by **2.5 m out** (`FadeStartM`/`FadeEndM` = 6/2.5, was 4/1), so an over-rotated gate entry (~5° off the taxi turn) finishes the squaring turn with room to creep straight in instead of cramming it into the final metre and stopping ~2° off.
- **Precise, unforgiving stop + persistent "docked" tone.** `StopToleranceMetres` tightened **0.5 → 0.3 m** (drives gate IsStop, the solid tone, and the "GSX docking complete." callout), so the pilot lands within ~0.3 m of the exact stop. The beep plateau is removed: `BeepNearMetres = StopToleranceMetres`, so the accelerating pulse keeps speeding up right to the stop with NO max-speed plateau — the old 2 m plateau made everything from 2 m to the stop sound identical, so pilots read "fast beep" as "stop" and parked short, mid-turn. Now: accelerating pulse = keep creeping; solid tone = stop here. The SOLID continuous tone was previously DEAD CODE — the state machine called `_beeper.Stop()` at the same 0.3 m threshold the solid tone begins, so the beep just vanished at the stop. Fixed: at IsStop the lateral pan tone stops but the beeper is held in its solid mode and KEEPS sounding through the Stopped state as a "docked — hold position" marker, until the pilot ends guidance (Stop taxi guidance button → `SetDestinationGate(null)` → `ResetLocked` stops it) or taxis/backs away (see the lifecycle bullet below). An OVERSHOOT stop does NOT hold the solid tone — a "docked" marker over a bad park misleads — and no longer disposes the beeper, so a back-up-and-retry dock re-engages with working audio.
- **Docking state lifecycle — Stopped is escapable, every state is exitable.** (a) **Taxi-away disengage uses ABSOLUTE distance, not along-track**: along-track goes NEGATIVE once the stop is behind the aircraft, so the old `alongM > 75` check could never fire for a forward taxi-out and the state (and solid tone) latched forever — raw distance >75 m disengages in ANY direction, including a stale next-flight gate hundreds of km away. (b) **Backing up >3 m past the stop re-arms to Idle** (`RearmBackupMetres`) so a back-up-and-retry dock re-engages through the normal `ShouldEngage` path with fresh audio + milestones. (c) **Disabling docking (or losing the gate) mid-approach fully resets** (`ResetLocked`, not just silence) — leaving `_state` latched at Docking/Stopped kept `IsActive` true forever, muting taxi's steering tone with no lateral cue for the final gate turn. (d) **Stopped-short closure**: engaged + sitting still ≥4 s with 0.3–10 m to go → *"X to stop. Continue forward."* — taxi's stopped-in-zone "Stop. Hold position." cue is suppressed while docking owns the arrival, so docking must provide its own closure instead of an endless fast-but-not-solid beep. (e) **Stale-gate lifecycle**: takeoff-assist activation and `LandingRollout` entry both call `SetDestinationGate(null)` — a stale departure gate could otherwise keep `IsActive` latched on landing and mute the landing-exit rollout steering tone.
- **Gate-lineup "aligned" band is docking-aware; gate lineup NEVER pulses.** Tight (1° / 12.5 ft enter, 2° / 25 ft exit) ONLY while docking is engaged (`_dockingActive` — docking's tone + 0.3 m stop own the precision and taxi's verbal is suppressed anyway); forgiving (4° / 25 ft enter, 7° / 40 ft exit) otherwise, because the navdata parking point is routinely metres off the real stand and demanding ~12 ft to it left correctly-parked pilots permanently "not aligned" (no "Parking brake." cue). The runway-style stopped-misaligned pulse was briefly enabled for gate lineup and is REMOVED — precision parking is docking's job, and pulsing 3 Hz at a correctly-parked pilot demanding precision to a possibly-offset navdata point is a misfeature. Runway lineup keeps its pulse (its centerline reference is authoritative). Do not re-add a gate pulse.
- **Hot-path perf invariants (do not regress):** docking far-field telemetry + lineup math are gated to `<150 m` raw distance or engaged (`DetailRangeMetres`) — no more 2/s `docking.log` file appends on the SimConnect thread, under the docking lock, for the whole taxi; hold-short label formatting happens only in firing branches and the hold-short/parking/exit-approach/runway-end callout paths early-out once all their latches have fired (don't reintroduce per-frame milestone-table builds); `TaxiAssistForm`'s gate list is cached per ICAO as (spot, resolved node) pairs and the search box / fit filter filter IN MEMORY per keystroke (don't reintroduce per-keystroke `GetGates` + navdata query + nearest-node resolution on the UI thread — matches the `GateTeleportForm` pattern); `SettingsManager.Save` serializes under the static lock but writes the file OUTSIDE it (don't move the IO back under the lock — an options-dialog save mid-approach stalled the 30 Hz position path behind an antivirus-scanned `%APPDATA%` write).
- **`docking.log` telemetry includes absolute coords.** Lines now carry `stopLat`/`stopLon` (computed stop target) and `acLat`/`acLon` (aircraft position) alongside the relative `along`/`crossFt`, so docking's target can be compared directly against a known-correct GSX position.
- **SimConnect heading-unit gotcha (live verification).** SimConnect's `PLANE_HEADING_DEGREES_TRUE` / `_MAGNETIC` are returned in **RADIANS**, not degrees, despite the name — multiply by 57.2958 (180/π) to get degrees (a logged 5.93 = 339.7°). Latitude/Longitude ARE in degrees. Applies to any future MCP/SimConnect live-verification of docking.
- **GSX operational note: engines OFF for services.** GSX will not offer ground services (deboarding/jetway/etc.) while engines are running — it prompts "stop engines to request services." This is GSX behaviour, not an MSFSBA bug; a precise dock with engines running still won't show service options.
- **Verified live (EDDF A66 / B77W, engines off):** offset 5.30 m applied; docking target (50.04691716, 8.56034700) heading 339.9° true; a real dock stopped ~0.6 m short + 0.27 m left of centerline and GSX accepted services — confirming the target is GSX-correct.
- **Distance units (`Settings/DistanceUnit.cs`, `Services/DistanceFormatter.cs`, `Services/DistanceMilestones.cs`).** Default metres, optional feet. `DistanceFormatter` is the DISPLAY layer only — its `UnitProvider` is wired to `SettingsManager.Current.GroundDistanceUnit` at startup (`MainForm`); **never use it for guidance thresholds** (those stay unit-native internally). `DistanceMilestones` returns **unit-native** countdown tables (round numbers in the active unit, e.g. docking 30/20/10/5 m vs 100/60/30/15 ft — NOT literal conversions); triggers stay metric so guidance logic is unaffected. **`GroundTrafficUseMetres` is a SEPARATE, independent toggle** — do not fold it into `GroundDistanceUnit`. **Long taxi distances (>~6000 ft, `TaxiGuidanceManager.FormatDistance`) switch to the big unit MATCHING the setting** — kilometres in metres mode, nautical miles in feet mode; a metric user never hears NM for a ground distance.

### Visual Landing Guidance (dual-tone)

**Audio rendering of PID output uses TWO `AudioToneGenerator` instances**, not one. Both always play. The DESIRED tone encodes the PID-commanded pitch (default 200–800 Hz over ±6°) and bank (stereo pan over ±5°); the CURRENT tone mirrors the same mapping against the aircraft's *actual* pitch/bank. Frequency match = correct pitch attitude (= correct VS on the 3° glideslope); pan match = correct bank. The pilot zero-beats the two by ear.

- **Visual guidance does NOT require HandFly mode.** It monitors its own attitude via `VISUAL_GUIDANCE_PITCH` and `VISUAL_GUIDANCE_BANK` events on the `VISUAL_GUIDANCE_DATA` callback (added to the struct alongside position / altitude / ground-track). Do NOT reintroduce a `!handFlyManager.IsActive` gate — that was the original design and pilots reported the three-tone overlap (HandFly's single tone + VG's two tones) made it impossible to tell which to follow.
- **HandFly tone is auto-muted while VG is active.** `MainForm.OnVisualGuidanceActiveChanged(true)` calls `handFlyManager.SuppressAudio()`; the `false` path calls `ResumeAudio()`. HandFly's announcements still fire if its feedback mode wants them — only the audio tone is muted. Do NOT remove this — VG's two tones use the same Hz/pan mapping as HandFly's tone, so playing all three together is acoustically incoherent.
- **The quick-access hotkey set (H, V, Q, S, D, B, P, A, F) is shared between HandFly and VG** via reference-counted registration. Both `RegisterHandFlyHotkeys` and `RegisterVisualGuidanceHotkeys` call `AcquireQuickAccessHotkeys` which increments a counter and registers any not-yet-held keys; the matching `Release` decrements and only unregisters when count hits zero. VG users get the SAME readout keys HandFly users do, because VG is hand-flying with extra guidance. Do NOT split the registration back into per-mode key sets — that's what created the double-register conflict the refactor fixed. The unified WM_HOTKEY dispatch (`if (handFlyHotkeysActive || visualGuidanceHotkeysActive)`) maps each key directly to its `HotkeyAction`; the action handlers self-gate where needed (e.g., `ReadTargetFPM` says "Visual guidance not active" when pressed in HandFly-only mode).
- **There is no single-tone mode for VG.** Both VG tones always run when visual guidance is active. Users who want the current tone less prominent should lower its volume in the Hand Fly Options dialog, not gate it off. Do NOT reintroduce a `VisualGuidanceCurrentToneEnabled` flag — the dual-tone IS the design.
- **Always route `cachedBank` through `VisualGuidanceManager.StandardBank(double)` before passing it to any tone API or computing a bank error.** SimConnect's `PLANE_BANK_DEGREES` is left-positive; `AudioToneGenerator` is right-positive. The PID's `desiredBank` output is already right-positive so it passes through raw — but `cachedBank` is the raw SimConnect value. `StandardBank` just returns `-simConnectBank`; its job is to make every call site self-documenting and obvious if the conversion is missing. `HandFlyManager.cs:155` does its own inline negation (different code path; left alone).
- **`VisualGuidanceManager.Initialize` is idempotent.** It calls `Stop()` first if either tone is still alive. Don't remove that guard; future callers might bypass `Toggle`'s strict on/off flow.
- **Tone Start() is deferred until the first ProcessUpdate.** `Initialize` instantiates both `AudioToneGenerator` instances and calls `Configure(...)` with the airframe's frequency mapping, but does NOT `Start()`. `StartTonesIfNeeded` inside `ProcessUpdate` kicks off WaveOut once real attitude commands exist, so the first audible note already reflects the airplane's state. Do not re-add a `Start()` call in Initialize; the deferral is what prevents the brief 500 Hz fused-tone glitch.
- **Start the current (follower) tone only if the desired tone started.** Without a reference, the follower plays a constant centre-pan tone forever — annoying and meaningless. `StartTonesIfNeeded` enforces this; don't reorder its try blocks.
- **Visual guidance auto-deactivates on the airborne→on-ground edge** in `MainForm.cs`'s `SIM_ON_GROUND` handler. From touchdown the landing-exit planner and taxi guidance take over the rollout and taxi audio respectively; running visual guidance alongside them would compete audibly. Manual activation on the ramp is still permitted (preflight test, etc.); only the edge transition triggers auto-deactivation. Do not gate this on GS or any other condition — landings of any speed should trigger it.
- **Aircraft-specific tone frequency / attitude range lives on `VisualGuidanceProfile`** (`ToneMinFrequencyHz`, `ToneMaxFrequencyHz`, `TonePitchRangeDeg`, `ToneBankRangeDeg`). Visual-guidance defaults are deliberately narrower than `AudioToneGenerator`'s native 10°/10°: pitch ±6° (50 Hz/° matching slope), bank ±5° (0.20 pan/°). The PMDG 777 widens `TonePitchRangeDeg` back to 10° (30 Hz/° — gentler beat at small errors during a stabilized approach). Override per airframe for aerobatic / fighter / glider envelopes that would saturate during normal manoeuvring.
- **Visual guidance has a hard-pan setting** (`VisualGuidanceHardPanTone`) mirroring the taxi/takeoff hard-pan options. Applied via `ApplyBank(tone, bank)` to BOTH tones in lockstep, so they still align when bank commands match. Snap deadband is ±1° standard convention.
- **Do not split lateral and vertical into separate tones.** The matching idiom relies on one oscillator per role (desired + current). Splitting would force the pilot to track four streams instead of two.
- **Default waveforms must differ between desired and current** (triangle + sine). Identical-waveform pure tones at the same frequency phase-cancel exactly at the matched state — the moment the pilot most needs them distinguishable.
- **Aircraft-specific tunables live on `IAircraftDefinition.GetVisualGuidanceProfile()`** — approach AoA, reference Vref, pitch-rate cap, bank-rate cap, tone frequency/attitude ranges, and the two glidepath-calibration biases below. A320 is the default; `PMDG777Definition` overrides for the heavy widebody (4.5° AoA, 2.0°/s pitch cap, 80 ft / 40 ft glidepath biases, 40 ft flare trigger, 4.5° flare target pitch, 10° tone pitch range). Do NOT bake aircraft-specific numbers back into `VisualGuidanceManager` as consts; that's the bug the profile was added to fix.
- **Glidepath altitude calibration — `GlideslopeAltitudeBiasFt` + `FlareAltitudeBiasFt` on `VisualGuidanceProfile`.** VG's altitude is the SimConnect reference datum (`PLANE ALTITUDE − threshold elevation`), and a bare `distance × tan(3°)` glidepath crosses the threshold at 0 ft — but a real ILS crosses at the ~50 ft reference datum height (TCH). Uncorrected, a coupled autoland reads as ~80 ft "high" on the 777 and VG's commanded vertical speed biases into excess descent. `GlideslopeAltitudeBiasFt` is **added to the ideal glidepath** (`idealAltitudeAGL = distance·tan(3°) + bias`) so VG's "on glideslope" matches the real ILS. `FlareAltitudeBiasFt` is **subtracted from the measured altitude** before the flare (30 ft) and touchdown (5 ft) phase thresholds, so the flare cue fires at true main-gear height instead of ~one bias too late (and so touchdown actually triggers — on a widebody the un-corrected datum never reaches 5 ft). The two are applied in **different code paths** (glideslope-error vs phase-detection) and were measured separately — do NOT collapse them into one shared constant. 777 values (80 / 40) are measured against a coupled autoland (the flare bias was bumped 20 → 30 → 40 across three test runs as each step moved the fire-point up by exactly 10 ft, confirming the real flare-attitude datum-vs-gear offset is 40 ft on the 777); A320 values (60 / 12) are estimates pending in-sim calibration. **`FlareTriggerWheelHeightFt`** is the true gear height at which the flare cue fires — per-aircraft because autoland and FCTM initiation heights differ (A320 = 30 ft default, 777 = 40 ft to match the autopilot's autoland). **`FlareTargetPitchDeg`** is the pitch commanded during the flare phase — per-aircraft because manufacturer flare attitudes differ (A320 default 6° per FCTM, 777 = 4.5° per Boeing FCTM's "2–3° pitch increase from approach attitude" guidance applied to the 777's ~1.5° approach pitch). **Every concrete aircraft declares its own `GetVisualGuidanceProfile()` override** — `FlyByWireA320Definition`, `FenixA320Definition`, and `PMDG777Definition` each spell out a full profile, so the math is explicitly keyed per airframe and FBW / Fenix glidepath biases can be calibrated independently of each other. The base `BaseAircraftDefinition` default is only a fallback for aircraft with no VG tuning. The Fenix A320's approach AoA / Vref / rate caps are the values validated in earlier flight testing — do not change them; only its glidepath biases are still estimates.
- **Glideslope angle is per-runway** (read from `ils.gs_pitch` in the navdata; cached on `Runway.GlideslopeAngleDeg`). Most ILSes are 3°, but London City is 5.5°, Aspen 6.59°, Innsbruck 3.8°, etc. — VG uses the published angle and falls back to 3° only when the runway has no ILS row, the DB build doesn't carry the angle, or the value falls outside the `[2°, 8°]` sanity band (defensive against corrupt navdata; Aspen at 6.59° is the steepest certified Cat I in the world). The angle feeds the ideal glidepath, the natural-descent-rate FPM target, the phase-capture deviation, and the nominal-pitch baseline — all four use the same per-runway value so they agree. The `MAX_DESCENT_RATE_FPM = -1500` safety clamp becomes **dynamic** (`min(-1500, natural × 1.3)`) so the legitimate per-runway descent profile is never clipped at steep approaches.
- **Nominal pitch baseline uses LIVE measured angle of attack**, not a static per-aircraft constant. `VisualGuidanceManager` subscribes to SimConnect `INCIDENCE ALPHA` via the existing `VISUAL_GUIDANCE_DATA` struct and uses the (EMA-smoothed, sanity-banded `[-5°, 20°]`) reading to compute `nominalPitch = -glideslopeAngleDeg + measuredAoaDeg`. Live AoA inherently encodes weight + flap + speed, so the nominal converges on whatever the airplane is actually trimmed for — no per-configuration look-up needed and the per-aircraft `TypicalApproachAoaDeg` is only a fallback for sim glitches or pre-first-sample frames. Smoothed AoA is preserved across out-of-band excursions so a single bad sample doesn't drop us back to the fallback.
- **Pitch PID has positive coefficients on `fpmError` / `fpmErrorRate`** (NOT the leading `-` that was historically there). Verified sign: with autothrust holding airspeed, MORE pitch ⇒ LESS descent. So negative `fpmError` (descending less than target ⇒ need more descent) calls for a NEGATIVE pitch correction ⇒ correction has the SAME sign as `fpmError`. The old `-fpmError * gain` produced wrong-direction guidance that was masked by autopilot tests (tight tracking ⇒ `fpmError ≈ 0` ⇒ the wrong-sign correction was negligible) and would have steered a manually-flying pilot away from the glideslope. Do NOT reintroduce the leading minus.
- **Threshold elevation is per-runway-end** (`runway_end.altitude`, cached on `Runway.ThresholdElevation`). At airports with sloped runways or different elevations between ends (KASE, LSZS, KSEA 16L/34R) this differs from the airport's published field elevation. Falls back to `airport.Altitude` only when the runway value is unknown.
- **PID math, phase machine, and lateral arc-capture logic are untouched** by the dual-tone work; the glidepath altitude calibration above is the one deliberate vertical-guidance change (a constant offset that shifts where "on glideslope" sits, not a gain/dynamics change). Failure mode of the new tone is a missing audible reference, never a wrong steering command — keep it that way.
- **Manual-query grace window.** When the pilot fires a readout hotkey (the H/V/Q/S/D/B/P/A/F set) while VG is active, `MainForm` calls `visualGuidanceManager.NotifyManualQuery()`, which suppresses the per-second bank-guidance and centerline-deviation callouts (both `AnnounceImmediate`) for 3 s so the readout isn't cut off mid-sentence. Only those two chatty callouts are suppressed — phase changes and distance callouts (rare one-shots) still fire. Skipped callouts lose nothing: both always reflect current state, so the next one carries fresh data. `IsManualReadoutAction` in `MainForm` lists the qualifying hotkey actions.

Details: [docs/visual-guidance.md](docs/visual-guidance.md).

### Multi-Aircraft Architecture

**Core interfaces:**
- **IAircraftDefinition** - Contract for all aircraft
- **BaseAircraftDefinition** - Recommended base class (provides hotkey routing, caching, helpers)
- **FlyByWireA320Definition** - Reference implementation

**Each aircraft defines:**
- `GetVariables()` - All simulator variables
- `GetPanelStructure()` - Section/panel hierarchy
- `BuildPanelControls()` - Panel-to-variables mapping (cached automatically by base class)
- `GetHotkeyVariableMap()` - Simple hotkey action → event name mappings
- `HandleHotkeyAction()` - Custom hotkey logic (optional override)

## Quick Reference

### Adding Panel Control
1. Add to aircraft's `GetVariables()` with `UpdateFrequency.OnRequest`
2. Add variable key to `BuildPanelControls()` under appropriate panel
3. Test - automatic registration and UI generation

### Adding Background Monitoring
1. Add to `GetVariables()` with `UpdateFrequency.Continuous` + `IsAnnounced = true`
2. Do NOT add to `BuildPanelControls()` - batched monitoring is automatic
3. Change detection and announcements are automatic (supports 1000 variables)

### Adding New Aircraft
1. Create class inheriting `BaseAircraftDefinition`
2. Override: `GetVariables()`, `GetPanelStructure()`, `BuildPanelControls()`
3. Add menu item in `MainForm.Designer.cs` + click handler
4. Add to `LoadAircraftFromCode()` switch statement
5. Use `FlyByWireA320Definition.cs` as template

### Variable Types
- **K:EVENT** - Standard MSFS events (via SimConnect TransmitClientEvent)
- **L:VARIABLE** - Local variables (reading aircraft state)
- **H:EVENT** - Hardware events (via MobiFlight WASM module)
- **PMDGVar** - PMDG SDK variables (read via Client Data Area broadcast)

### `SimConnectManager.SetLVar` — GLOBAL MobiFlight calc-path routing (2026-06)

**Every L:var write that reaches `SetLVar` is routed through the MobiFlight calculator path (`ExecuteCalculatorCode("{v} (>L:{var})")`) when MobiFlight is connected** — NOT the native `AddToDataDefinition` + `SetDataOnSimObject` write (which is unreliable for many add-on L:vars and silently reverts FBW vars a frame later). The routing lives in `SetLVar` (`SimConnectManager.cs` ~3896) and is gated:
- **`CalcPathVerified`** must be true (the end-to-end nonce probe — `IsMobiFlightConnected` is true even with NO WASM module installed, so it must never gate writes) — otherwise it falls through to the data-def write so users without the WASM module still work; FBW installs verify within ~3 s of detection.
- **Plain L:var names only** — a name containing a **space or colon** is a stock SimVar shape (`TRANSPONDER STATE:1`, `INTERACTIVE POINT OPEN:0`) and is left on the data-def path; `SetLVar` always prepends `L:` so a real caller never passes such a name through the calc branch.

**So "with MobiFlight connected, does everything use the calc path except PMDG?" — essentially YES for L:var writes, with the precise scope being:**
- **Routed through the calc path:** every plain-L:var write — panel combos/buttons (MainForm's `if (!handled) SetLVar(...)` fallback, ~MainForm.cs:5179/5217/5323/5484), the FBW per-prefix catch-alls, and every aircraft def's `SetLVar(key,value)` call (Fenix combos, etc.).
- **NOT routed (use their own mechanism regardless of MobiFlight):** **PMDG** (writes via CDA `SetClientData`/`SendPMDGEvent` — never calls `SetLVar`), **K-events** (`SendEvent`/`TransmitClientEvent`), **H-events**, and **stock SimVars** (space/colon names, left on data-def). HS787 control writes are K/H-events, also unaffected.

**`SendEvent` H:/dotted calc-path gate + pre-connection queue.** The H:/dotted FBW event classes (e.g. `H:A380X_EFIS_CP_BARO_PUSH_1`, `A32NX.FCU_AP_1_PUSH`) prefer the MobiFlight calc path. `SendEvent` splits them: **H: events** go to the MobiFlight channel whenever `IsMobiFlightConnected` (queued during the brief connect window — they have no other transport on any branch). **Dotted events** prefer the calc path only once **`CalcPathVerified`**; while the probe is still running they are queued in the bounded `pendingCalcEvents` (cap `MaxPendingCalcEvents = 64`), then flushed via calc on `MarkCalcPathVerified` or via the legacy `MapClientEventToSimEvent` + `TransmitClientEvent` transport on `MarkCalcPathProbeConcluded` (module absent, or a non-FBW aircraft that can't probe — MainForm concludes immediately for those). The queue is cleared on MobiFlight teardown so events never carry across a disconnect/aircraft swap. `FireCalcEvent` is the shared single-event dispatcher used by both the live path and the flush.

**Catch-all standardization across aircraft — the verdict (verified, do NOT "fix" the Fenix):** the per-control explicit cases in `FenixA320Definition.HandleUIVariableSet` are **fine, not a gap**. MainForm ALREADY provides the effective catch-all: when `HandleUIVariableSet` returns false, the combo/button paths call `SetLVar(varKey, value)` (now calc-routed). So a plain Fenix L:var combo works with NO explicit case at all. The explicit Fenix cases that *matter* are the ones doing MORE than a plain write — button transitions (`ExecuteButtonTransition`, 0→1 pulse), COM frequency (validate + Hz + `SendEvent`), and encoder increment/decrement counters — and those **cannot** be replaced by a blanket `SetLVar` catch-all without breaking. A single cross-aircraft catch-all is impossible: **PMDG** (CDA struct offsets, inversions, momentary params) and **HS787** (K/H-event tables) don't write L:vars at all, so a string-keyed `SetLVar` catch-all is meaningless for them. The standard already exists at the MainForm `SetLVar`-fallback layer; each def only adds explicit cases for non-plain-write controls.

**RPN number formatting must be invariant fixed-point** — `value.ToString("0.################", InvariantCulture)` (or `"0.###"`-style) — NEVER default `{0}` formatting or `$"{double}"` interpolation: the former emits scientific notation for small/large magnitudes (`1E-05`) and the latter uses CurrentCulture (`87,5` on comma-decimal locales); the MSFS RPN parser rejects both. Same rule for every `ExecuteCalculatorCode` call that embeds a computed double (the A380 temp-selector was bitten).

### Fenix A320 cockpit controls — new "Cockpit" panel section (2026-06)

`FenixA320Definition.GetPanelStructure` has a **"Cockpit"** section with 5 panels exposing 24 previously-uncovered, live-verified-settable L:var combos (all route through `SetLVar` → the MobiFlight calc path):
- **Captain Seat / First Officer Seat** — Seat Height (`S_SEAT_HEIGHT_*`), Seat Distance (`S_SEAT_DISTANCE_*`), Armrest L/R (`S_ARMREST_{LEFT,RIGHT}_*`). Seats are **3-position direction switches** (Height: Down/Stop/Up; Distance: Aft/Stop/Forward) that HOLD the written value — the seat moves while at Down/Up (0/2) and the model **auto-centers the switch to Stop (1) at the travel limit** (no per-frame motor-tick needed, unlike the A380's `SEAT_*_MOVE_*` 0-100 position vars). The Height/Distance combos are `Continuous+IsAnnounced` so they track that spring-to-Stop silently (see the monitor section); armrests are `OnRequest` (2-position, no Stop).
- **Windows and Shades** — sunshades + window blinds (`S_SUNSHADE_*`, `S_WINDOW_BLINDS_*`).
- **Standby Instruments** — `S_STANDBY_COMPASS`, `S_STANDBY_ATTITUDE_CAGE`.
- **Cockpit Other** — jumpseat + headrest, cockpit-door video, oxygen-mask covers, gravity-gear extension + crank, F/O DCDU brightness. (NOTE: the overhead emergency-call guard `S_OH_CALLS_EMER_Cover` is NOT here — it was already defined+paneled in the overhead Calls panel; an early duplicate was removed.)

**DEFERRED Fenix cockpit controls** (need different handling than a plain `SetLVar` combo — implement as `RenderAsButton` pulses / increment events): the **momentary buttons** — cockpit-door unlock/lock, the clock buttons (`S_MIP_CLOCK_CHR/ET/RST/SET/UTC`), the DCDU2 keypad (LSK/MSG/PG/PRINT — control-only since the DCDU2 display isn't readable), `S_MIP_ISFD_BARO_BUTTON`, `S_PED_DFDR_EVENT`, `S_PED_AIDS_PRINT`, `OH_RCRD_GND_CTL`; the **encoders** (`E_STANDBY_ALT_IMPERIAL_BARO`, `E_STANDBY_ALT_METRIC_BARO`, `E_MIP_CLOCK_SET`); and **uncertain-semantics** controls left out on purpose (`S_AUDIO_SWITCHING` accepts 1/2 not 0; `S_CHART_LIGHT_TEMP_CAPT/FO`).

### Fenix monitor manager (Ctrl+M) — now DYNAMIC + clock counters default-off (2026-06)

`FenixMonitorManagerForm` previously listed a **hardcoded 10 keys** (master warnings/cautions + ECAM CLR) — the "weird version". It now enumerates **every `UpdateFrequency.Continuous + IsAnnounced` var** from the aircraft def (mirroring `FBWA380MonitorManagerForm` / `FlyByWireA320MonitorManagerForm`), sorted by display name. Unchecked keys persist to `UserSettings.FenixDisabledMonitorVariables`; `MainForm.OnSimVarUpdated` (~683) already gates on it. Most Fenix cockpit controls (comfort/standby/gravity-gear etc.) are `OnRequest` panel combos — not monitor entries — EXCEPT the 4 seat height/distance switches, which are `Continuous+IsAnnounced` (so the combo can track the spring-to-Stop) but seeded default-silent (see below).

**Default-silenced (monitored but not spoken) vars** — seeded once into `FenixDisabledMonitorVariables` by `SettingsManager.SeedFenixMonitorDefaults` (called from `Load`, guarded by `UserSettings.FenixMonitorDefaultsSeeded`; the user can re-enable any in Ctrl+M, and the flag stops re-seeding after a deliberate re-enable):
- **`N_MIP_CLOCK_CHRONO` / `N_MIP_CLOCK_ELAPSED`** — raw-seconds counters (`IsAnnounced`, no ValueDescriptions) that tick every second → pure announce spam ("CLOCK CHRONO: 3723").
- **The 4 seat height/distance switches** (`S_SEAT_{HEIGHT,DISTANCE}_{CAPT,FO}`) — these were changed from `OnRequest` to **`Continuous + IsAnnounced`** specifically so the panel **combo can track the spring-to-Stop** (the Fenix model auto-centers the 3-position switch to Stop=1 at the travel limit; an `OnRequest` combo kept showing the stale "Up"). They must be `Continuous+IsAnnounced` to be live-monitored (SimConnect only batches `Continuous+IsAnnounced` vars), but the user wanted the value WITHOUT speech — so they're seeded silent. **This works because the combo update (`MainForm.UpdateControlFromSimVar`, ~660) runs BEFORE the disabled-monitor announce gate (~683) in `OnSimVarUpdated`** — the combo's `SelectedIndex` snaps to "Stop" while the announce is skipped. The armrests stay `OnRequest` (2-position, no Stop to spring to). User-set changes don't feed back (`updatingFromSim` guard).

### PMDG 777 Specific Patterns

**Switch control:** Use CDA (SetClientData) with direct position values for most switches.
- Two-position toggles: `SendPMDGEvent(eventName, eventId, targetPosition)` where targetPosition is 0 or 1
- Multi-position selectors: same, with the target position index
- Momentary buttons: `SendPMDGEvent(eventName, eventId, 1)` — parameter 1 = pressed, 0 = no-op
- Continuous knobs (brightness, temperature, EFIS baro/mins): **cannot be controlled via the SDK event with a position param** — do not add to panels via that path. **EXCEPTION (2026-06): knobs whose cockpit-model L:var IS the pilot input are fully settable by writing that named L:var** — e.g. the shoulder heaters (`L:LEFT/RIGHT_SHOULDER_HEATER`, 0–100; the SDK struct field `AIR_ShoulderHeaterKnob` follows the write, live-verified). Find the L:var in `77W_Cockpit_Behavior.xml`; see the Cockpit furniture section below.
- **Fuel control levers:** Exception — use CDA with **inverted** parameter (1=Cutoff, 0=Run). See special case in HandleUIVariableSet.
- **Ground power switches (ELEC_ExtPwr):** Momentary push buttons — send parameter 1 regardless of target. See special case in HandleUIVariableSet.

**Cockpit furniture (777 "Cockpit" panel section — Captain/FO Seat, Windows and Shades, Doors and Tables; all live-verified 2026-06-11):** Two mechanism families, both discovered by reading the cockpit behavior XML (`...\pmdg-aircraft-77w\SimObjects\Airplanes\PMDG 777-300ER\attachments\pmdg\Function_Interior_77W\model\77W_Cockpit_Behavior.xml` — the complete map of every interactive cockpit part and its L:vars):
- **SDK-event furniture** — armrests (`EVT_CA/FO_ARMREST_LEFT/RIGHT_SWITCH`, CDA param 1=up/0=down) and foot heaters (`EVT_FWD_LEFT/RIGHT_FOOT_HEATER`, direct position 0/1/2 + SDK struct read-back `AIR_FootHeaterSelector`). The armrest anim L:vars `switch_1006_a`–`switch_1009_a` are **PMDG-SDK-owned read-backs** (rewritten from the real switch state every frame, same family as the xBAW switches) — a raw SetLVar reverts; the event is the actuator and the L:var follows for the combo display. Generic rule: `switch_<eventOffset>_a` anim L:vars give read-back for SDK events with no struct field.
- **L:var-input furniture** — visors (`visor_{L,R}_{front,side}_stow_unstow` + `_drag`, 0–100), worktables (`worktable_{ca,fo,obs_l,obs_r}`), shoulder heaters, window handle/clipboard (`WindowHandle{CA,FO}` / `WindowClipboard{CA,FO}`), cockpit door (`door_cockpit` — flips the SDK `DOOR_CockpitDoorOpen` read-back), crew rest doors (`door_crew_area_{left,right}`), cockpit curtain (`curtain_cockpit`), window shades (`7X7X_shade_{LF,LR,RF,RR}`, bool). These L:vars ARE the pilot input: writes hold and the model/system follows, so plain combos via MainForm's generic `SetLVar` fall-through drive them — no event mapping.
- **Sliding windows are the special case** — NO PMDG event exists for the window itself; the cockpit click runs RPN that toggles `L:Window_OpenClose_{CA,FO}` and fires stock `TOGGLE_AIRCRAFT_EXIT_FAST` on **exit 17 (captain) / 18 (FO)**, gated on handle unlocked AND clipboard moved aside. The `WINDOW_CA/FO` combos replicate that callback verbatim via `ExecuteCalculatorCode`; **Open auto-performs the unlock sequence** (handle + clipboard to 100 first), Close only closes (the model blocks the handle while the window travels — re-lock via its combo afterwards).
- **Crew seats are NOT adjustable on the PMDG 777** — no event, no struct field, no L:var, no model animation (verified across SDK, behavior XML, and the gltf: seat meshes are static). The armrests are the entire movable-seat surface; don't go hunting for seat-motion vars.

**Radio frequencies and transponder:** Use standard SimConnect events (not PMDG SDK):
- `COM_STBY_RADIO_SET_HZ` / `COM2_STBY_RADIO_SET_HZ` for setting standby freqs
- `COM_STBY_RADIO_SWAP` / `COM2_RADIO_SWAP` for swapping active/standby
- `XPNDR_SET` for squawk code (BCD16 encoded)

**CDU array index convention:** The PMDG SDK uses `0=Captain(L), 1=F/O(R), 2=Observer(C)` for ALL crew-position arrays — including CDU data areas (`PMDG_777X_CDU_0/1/2`), `CDU_BrtKnob[3]`, and all `CDU_annun*[3]` fields. The CDU form dropdown is ordered Left/Center/Right (0/1/2), which does NOT match the SDK ordering. `PMDG777CDUForm` uses a `DataCDUIndex` computed property to remap dropdown index to SDK index (`1→2, 2→1`). The event prefix switch (`EVT_CDU_L_/C_/R_`) uses the raw dropdown index and is correct as-is.

**CDU interaction:** CDU buttons must send parameter 1 (pressed) via CDA; parameter 0 also registers as a press (not a release). Text entry sends one character at a time with 350ms delay; repeated characters need an extra 400ms for the CDU to distinguish separate presses. CDU display uses color and font-size data to detect toggle selections (non-white color or non-small font = selected, marked with `X`). Toggle detection only applies to rows with adjacent `<>` (mapped from 0xA1/0xA2 arrow symbols). Scratchpad announcements are suppressed during text entry and clearing (`_typingInProgress`/`_clearingInProgress` flags); `_previousScratchpad` is only updated when the announcement actually fires. CLR uses `_clearingInProgress` to suppress intermediate states and only announces "Cleared" once the scratchpad is empty.

**MCP dialogs:** Use `ValueInputForm` with `ToggleButtonDef` for mode toggles. Opened non-modal (`Show()`, not `ShowDialog()`) with `ShowCancelButton = false` so other windows remain accessible. Dialogs stay open after value entry (callback pattern). `MCP_IASBlank` indicates FMC-controlled speed. VS/FPA dialog uses `inputEnabledCheck` to gate input on mode engagement (`MCP_annunVS_FPA`). `EVT_MCP_VS_SET` requires VS mode to be engaged first ("VS window open").

**VS/FPA event naming (SDK names are misleading):** `EVT_MCP_VS_SWITCH` (69855) is the **engage/disengage** button. `EVT_MCP_VS_FPA_SWITCH` (69852) is the **VS↔FPA display mode toggle**. Confirmed by live sim testing — do not trust the SDK naming alone.

**Announcements:** Use `Announce()` (queued) in ProcessSimVarUpdate, `AnnounceImmediate()` only in HandleHotkeyAction. `IsAnnounced = true` is required for continuous monitoring registration. Suppress button push state (_Sw_Pushed) announcements via RenderAsButton check. Annunciator lights announce both on and off states. For variables needing cache but no auto-announcement, set `IsAnnounced = true` and return `true` from ProcessSimVarUpdate to suppress.

**System Display synoptic read-outs (`PMDG777Definition.SystemDisplay.cs`, partial class).** A read-only status box in the **Displays → System Display** panel, organized like the real Display Select Panel synoptic pages. A single combo (`PMDG777_SD_PAGE`, `SdPageKey`) selects one of 9 pages (0 Engine, 1 Status, 2 Electrical, 3 Hydraulics, 4 Fuel, 5 Air, 6 Doors, 7 Gear, 8 Flight Controls); selecting a page writes a private L:var (`PMDG777_MSFSBA_SD_PAGE`), and `RefreshSystemDisplayAsync` repaints the box. **HYBRID data sourcing** — each row is `(label, var, fmt)`: most values are **stock SimVars** read from the SimConnect cache (`GetCachedVariableValue` — oil temp/press/qty, EGT, N1/N2, fuel flow, hydraulic pressure/reservoir, electrical voltages, cabin alt/rate/diff, CG%MAC, gear, control surfaces/trim), while a small set of PMDG-SDK-broadcast fields (`_sdPmdgVars`: feed-tank fuel quantities, duct pressures, brake accumulator, IRS aligned, APU running, door states) are read **live** via `simConnect.PMDGDataManager.GetFieldValue(name)` (with `_N` array-index suffix), because OnRequest PMDGVars never land in the SimConnect cache. The box rides the GENERIC MainForm `_DISPLAY_`/`_REFRESH_` status-box infra (3 s caret-preserving auto-refresh) — `OnDisplayPanelShown` triggers a refresh when the panel is shown; `TryGetDisplayOverride(SdPageKey, …)` renders the page name + content. **Documented gaps not in the SDK** (so NOT covered): oxygen, water, brake temp, tire pressure, APU N/EGT/load, generator load amps, EICAS alert message TEXT (WASM-only), wear/cycles, chrono elapsed time.

### PMDG 737-800 NG3 Specific Patterns

Details: [docs/pmdg-737.md](docs/pmdg-737.md). Key gotchas: two CDUs (no observer), no FPA mode, annunciator names differ from 777 (LVL_CHG / HDG_SEL / VOR_LOC), DU selectors have "reverse sequence for FO", fire handles need an active fire to test, the 737 EFB has full parity with the 777 (Dashboard / Preferences / Navdata / Performance / Ground Ops / W&B / Manuals) via the shared `PMDGEFBForm`, opened with Shift+T — the EFB app is byte-identical across all four 737 variants and the 777, so one shared bridge JS + `zzz-pmdg-efb-accessibility` Community package serves them all.

### PMDG EFB (Coherent debugger)

The PMDG EFB tablet is read and driven over the MSFS Coherent GT remote debugger (`http://127.0.0.1:19999`), like the FBW A380 flyPad. NO Community mod package, NO HTTP bridge, NO HTML patching, and NO sim restart are required.

**Architecture:** `SimConnect/CoherentPmdgEfbClient.cs` (implements `IMcduBridge`) connects to the `PMDGTablet` Coherent view, installs the generic in-page agent `Resources/coherent-pmdg-efb-agent.js` (ES5: resolves controls by TYPE not element id, so new PMDG pages read automatically), and polls `scrape()` — capturing readable document TEXT (linearizing the SimBrief OFP `<pre>` briefing + NOTAMs), two-column label↔control pairing, checkbox active-unit from the EFB `Settings` object, fa-icon labeling, leaflet-marker skip, and duplicate-button id disambiguation. Transport: `CoherentPmdgEfbClient` exposes `click_mcdu_element(idx)` / `set_element_value(idx, text)` commands (same shape as FBW A320/A380). UI: reuses `Forms/FBWA380/FbwEfbForm.cs` WebView2 browse view (the same form the FBW flyPad uses), with a monospace `<pre>` render branch for the OFP. On startup, `Patching/LegacyEfbBridgeCleanup.cs` removes the retired Community packages (`zzz-pmdg-efb-accessibility`, `zzz-hs787-accessibility`) automatically.

**Noise-suppression / label-robustness rules in `collect()` (all live-validated 2026-06-20 against the 777 tablet, jsdom-locked in `tools/pmdg-efb-test`):**
- **Drop truly-anonymous buttons.** A button whose label resolves empty (no text, no fa-icon, no title/aria/id, no row-pair) is NOT emitted — after a SimBrief/weather load the Dashboard map sprouts unlabeled leaflet overlay/control buttons the `leaflet-marker-icon` skip misses; they'd read as a flood of "(button)". A button with an id still gets its id-derived name (so this only drops genuinely nameless ones).
- **Drop single-character glyph text.** Standalone text-content whose trimmed length ≤ 1 is a decorative graphic glyph, never content — the Take-Off page renders the runway designators "35R"/"17L" as per-character `<span>`s ("3","5","R","1","7","L") inside `#opt_takeoff_runway.runway_container`. Skipped BEFORE the same-row merge so "R"+"1" can't combine into "R 1". The real value still reads from the Runway ID dropdown.
- **A field label must contain letters.** `_rowLabel` skips value-DISPLAY labels (the weather widget renders Temp/Wind/Dewpoint/QNH as `<label class="pmdg_measurement">28</label>` — a value, not a field label) and requires the matched label to contain a letter; the two-column pairing applies the same letter-guard. Without this the "Toggle Weather" checkbox + "Weather Icao" field borrowed the METAR temperature ("28"/"31"). The id fallback then yields the correct "Toggle Weather"/"Weather Icao".
- **Icon-button collisions read clean id names.** When two icon-only buttons collide on a generic fa glyph (after a weather load BOTH the status-bar refresh and the weather-search button show fa "Refresh"), the disambiguation uses the descriptive id name AS the label ("Statusbar Restart" / "Weather Search") instead of the clunky "Weather Search Button: Refresh"; `idToLabel` also strips a redundant trailing "Button"/"Btn" word (the role is already announced). A button with real visible TEXT keeps the qualifier prefix (W&B "Pax Level: Randomize" stays distinct).

**Hotkeys:** **Shift+T = Captain tablet**, **Ctrl+Shift+T = First Officer tablet** (input mode, Shift+T output mode shows the EFB; Shift+T input mode on the PMDG 737/777 opens the EFB form). Shared across 737 + 777 (the EFB app is identical). Opened with Shift+T.

### FlyByWire A380X Specific Patterns

`FlyByWireA380Definition` (code `FBW_A380`), branch `fly-by-wire-A380-integration`.

**No-injection MCDU/flyPad transport.** The A380X MFD/MCDU and flyPad EFB are read AND driven live through the MSFS Coherent GT remote debugger (`http://127.0.0.1:19999`, WebKit inspector, `Runtime.evaluate`) — NOT via a Community-folder mod or HTTP bridge. `SimConnect/CoherentDebuggerClient.cs` (MFD, resolves the view by title needle `A380X_MFD`) and `SimConnect/CoherentEFBClient.cs` (flyPad, title needle `- EFB`) both implement `IMcduBridge`, so `FBWA380MCDUForm`/`FBWA380EFBForm` are transport-agnostic. The in-page agents are `Resources/coherent-a380-agent.js` and `coherent-flypad-agent.js` — **ES5 only** (Coherent GT = Chromium 49: `var`, no arrow funcs, no `String.includes`, top-level try/catch). MFD page-ids shift each session → always resolve by TITLE. **No Community-folder injection, no HTML patching, no sim restart** — the debugger is the sole A380 transport (all injection code was removed; PMDG still uses its own `EFBBridgeServer`). **Developer Mode is NOT required** — verified empirically on MSFS 2024 (cold boot, Dev Mode off): port 19999 is opened by the sim itself and `/pagelist.json` + the WebSocket `Runtime.evaluate` inspector protocol both work, so the debugger transport runs with no Dev Mode and no dev toolbar.

**flyPad = WebView2 "browser mode".** `FBWA380EFBForm` renders the scraped flyPad elements as a real semantic HTML document inside an embedded **WebView2** (already a dep; PMDG EFB precedent), so the screen reader gets native browse mode (H headings, K links, arrow-by-line, real `<input>`s, `aria-live` page-change). NO http server — `NavigateToString(PageHtml)` once, then `ExecuteScriptAsync("window.__render(<json>)")` per update; the page posts click/set/refresh back via `chrome.webview.postMessage` → `WebMessageReceived` → `EnqueueCommand`. The native flat-list is a SILENT auto-fallback only if WebView2 init fails (no user toggle). **Click index gotcha:** the agent's `clickElement`/`setValue` look up the STAMPED `data-fbwa380-efb-idx`, which diverges from the list position (the list is sorted+deduped after stamping) — so `CoherentEFBClient` carries it as `items.N.aidx` and the form sends THAT, not the loop index. **flyPad div-buttons:** many action buttons (e.g. modal Cancel/Confirm) are styled `<div>`s with no `button`/`btn` token or role — the agent classifies a `hover:`-styled leaf with its own short text as a button (interactive flyPad elements carry Tailwind `hover:` classes; static text never does). Value inputs (PAX/KGS) have no label metadata → `labelFor` reads the field's parent unit text before falling back to the section heading.

**ND OANS / BTV (Ctrl+Shift+B) — DATA-ONLY, ZERO-RENDER (2026-06, latest; supersedes all earlier scrape/TabControl OANS notes).** `Forms/FBWA380/FBWA380OansForm.cs` is a native WinForms `TabControl` (**Map and BTV / Airport / Status**) driven by `SimConnect/CoherentNDClient.cs` + `Resources/coherent-oans-agent.js` — but the agent is now **data-only**: it READS OANS/BTV state from the ND JS instance objects (`document.querySelector('a380x-nd').fsInstrument.oansRef.instance` → `btvUtils` / `labelManager.labels` / `fmsDataStore` / `dataAirportIcao` / `dataAirportName`) plus OANS L:vars, and WRITES via `btvUtils` methods + the msfs-sdk EventBus (`bus.pub`). **It NEVER writes `A32NX_EFIS_L_ND_RANGE`, forces panel `.style.visibility`, or scrapes the control-panel DOM.** ⚠️ The earlier `ensureAirportZoom`+DOM-scrape design forced a continuous full-airport map render on every poll and exhausted host commit memory (paging-file-too-small errors that froze the whole machine) — **do NOT reintroduce any forced render/zoom/visibility or DOM `scrape`/`enumerate`.** Agent API: `ping()`, `snapshot()` → `{ok,available,failed,airport,fms,btv,manual,airac}`, `armRunway(name)`, `armExit(name)`, `clearBtv()`, `displayAirport(icao)` (one-shot AMDB load — USER ACTION ONLY, never on a poll), `setManualStopDistance(m)`. The client polls `snapshot()` read-only (1 s), raises a dedup'd **`oans_state`** push (+ **`oans_connected`**), and exposes commands `get_snapshot` / `oans_arm_runway` / `oans_arm_exit` / `oans_clear` / `oans_display_airport` / `oans_set_manual_stop`. **Two tiers:** with Navigraph maps loaded (`A32NX_OANS_AVAILABLE=1`) the runway/exit pick-lists + arming + predicted dry/wet/live stop, ROT, turnaround and the runway-ahead QFU all work; without Navigraph the form shows a **Manual BTV** section — runway length (ARINC `A32NX_OANS_RWY_LENGTH`), type a stop distance → `oansManualStoppingDistance` bus pub, then "select the landing runway in the FMS". The top banner states which tier is active. **Visual-only OANS controls are intentionally REMOVED** (the RWY/TWY/STAND/OTHER entity picker, ADD CROSS/FLAG, CENTER MAP, the permanently-disabled LDG SHIFT) — they have no audio meaning for a blind pilot (STAND = parking stands, OTHER = de-icing areas — both map-locate-only). The runway-ahead advisory naming (`btvUtils.rwyAheadQfu`) shows in the window readout; an **always-on** named advisory (window closed) is deferred (it would need a persistent ND read socket — the generic SimVar `A32NX_OANS_WORD_1` bit-11 advisory in the def stays the always-on path). **Navigraph is user-side:** the AMDB airport maps are fetched from the online `https://amdb.api.navigraph.com` API using the user's Navigraph login in the flyPad EFB (Shift+T) — there is NO local file to fetch and MSFSBA must never try to; the aircraft loads the maps and MSFSBA reads what's loaded. **Exit pick-list is FILTERED to valid exits for the armed runway** — `snapshot().btv.exits` returns `agent.validExitsForArmed()`, a READ-ONLY (pure airport-local-metre math, NO canvas draw, NO mutation) verbatim port of FBW `OansBrakeToVacateSelection.selectExitFromOans`'s accept/reject test (400 m touchdown-zone, 50 m centerline, 120° gates; falls back to the full list only if the armed-runway threshold refs aren't set). Without it the combo listed all airport exits alphabetically and the first (e.g. OMDB K-series for rwy 12L) were silently rejected. **Multiple exit-line features can share ONE name (live-verified KSFO 28R / exit "Q", 2026-06): a taxiway often exposes a far-off-runway segment AND a valid on-runway one under the same text.** `validExitsForArmed` whitelists a NAME when ANY of its features passes (and sets the `seen` dedup only on ACCEPT, so an invalid first feature can't block a valid later one), so the list correctly shows "Q". But `armExit` used to pick the FIRST feature by name (`findLabel`) — at KSFO that was the off-runway "Q" (230 m off the 28R centerline) → `selectExitFromOans` rejected it → "Exit Q not valid … (wrong side or too close to threshold)" even though Q *was* valid. **FIX:** `armExit(name)` now iterates EVERY same-named exit-line feature and arms the first one `selectExitFromOans` accepts (mirroring a sighted pilot clicking the correct map label). **The per-feature `selectExitFromOans` call is wrapped in its OWN `try/continue` (not one try/catch around the whole loop)** — a throw on an early/malformed same-named feature must fall through to the next candidate, not abort the loop and reject a valid later feature; the last error is reported only if NO feature armed. Likewise `armRunway`'s threshold-search loop guards `feats[k] && feats[k].properties` (it runs outside the method's try, so an unguarded `.properties` deref on a partial AMDB feature would throw uncaught out of `armRunway`). This is SAFE re the memory rule below: it loops only over the 1–2 features sharing the SELECTED name (not all ~290 exits), and a REJECTED feature returns from `selectExitFromOans` BEFORE `drawBtvLayer` — so at most ONE canvas redraw (the accepted feature) occurs, same as before. **Exit list is sorted closest-first with distance:** `validExitsForArmed` returns `[{name, dist}]` sorted ascending by `dist` = the BTV exit distance in metres (raw threshold→exit minus the 400 m touchdown zone == `btvExitDistance`, so the pick-list and the armed-exit readout report the SAME number); the snapshot carries a parallel `btv.exitDists` array, and the form's exit combo items read "Q, 2,289 m / 7,510 ft" (unit per the metric toggle) so the screen reader announces how far down the runway each exit is while arrowing the dropdown. **Rejection feedback:** `EnqueueCommand` captures the arm result and raises `oans_action`; the form announces non-success results (e.g. "Exit K1 not valid for this runway …") so a rejected exit is never silent. ⚠️ NEVER loop `armExit`/`armRunway` over the FULL exit list (~290 calls) — each ACCEPTED arm triggers a BTV canvas redraw and a tight full-sweep exhausts host memory; the validity FILTER above is the read-only way to enumerate valid exits (arming only the 1–2 same-named features, as the fix does, is fine). **Loading an airport: call `oansRef.instance.loadAirportMap(icao)` DIRECTLY, NOT the `oans_display_airport` bus event.** When the OANS is in performance-hide mode (FBW perf mode on + the ND not rendering the OANS — the normal case for us since we never render), the `oans_display_airport` handler (Oanc.tsx) only sets `dataAirportIcao` and SKIPS the load, leaving the ICAO showing with `data===undefined` / 0 labels / `btvReady` false (symptom: "(KLAX)" with no runway list). `agent.displayAirport()` therefore calls `loadAirportMap(icao)` directly (bus pub is the fallback), which loads the AMDB + builds labels regardless of perf-hide (live-verified KLAX → 4789 features / 828 labels, persists; `getAirportData` itself was never the problem). Same gate disables the cockpit auto-load under perf-hide, so the user must press "Display airport" (or Origin/Dest/Alternate) to load — the banner says "maps available — load an airport" until they do.

**Accessible BTV exit arming — native combos + buttons + auto-announce (2026-06, live-verified at VCBI).** On the real A380 you SELECT the BTV landing runway + exit by **clicking the runway-end + exit LABELS on the moving map** (`Oanc.tsx` → `btvUtils.selectRunwayFromOans` / `selectExitFromOans`). Those are SVG on the map canvas with no control-panel widget, so a blind pilot cannot reach them — and selecting RWY/TWY in the control panel only filters the *map*, it does not arm BTV (the user's "if i select rway nothing is shown" / "can't select taxiways after the landing runway is selected" — that dropdown is a map-filter, not an arming control). **`coherent-oans-agent.js` calls the same `btvUtils` methods directly** via the ND instrument instance (`document.querySelector('a380x-nd').fsInstrument.oansRef.instance` → `btvUtils`):
- `oanc()` / `btvReady()`; `btvRunwayList()` / `btvExitList()` (from `labelManager.labels` filtered by `associatedFeature.feattype`: RunwayThreshold=2, runway-centerline=4, RunwayExitLine=19);
- `armRunway(name)` (finds the centerline label + the `data.features` threshold with `idthr===name`, calls `selectRunwayFromOans(icao+name, centerline.associatedFeature, threshold)`); `armExit(name)` (requires a runway armed first; `selectExitFromOans(name, exitLabel.associatedFeature)` — returns "wrong side / too close to threshold" if FBW rejects it); `clearBtv()`;
- `snapshot().btv → `{ready, runways:[], exits:[], runway, exit, lda, exitDist, dry, wet, stop, computing}` — the pick-lists, the armed runway/exit (these are **NOT L:vars**, only OANS observables `btvRunway`/`btvExit`/`btvRunwayLda`/`btvExitDistance`), and the predicted **DRY / WET / live STOP-bar** distances read from the plain-metre L:vars `A32NX_OANS_BTV_{DRY,WET,STOP_BAR}_DISTANCE_ESTIMATED` (0 until the FMS computes the landing on approach; stop-bar only surfaced once dry/wet compute, since it carries a ~40 m ground offset).
`snapshot()` returns the BTV block (data-only — see the zero-render note above). `CoherentNDClient` parses it (`Snapshot.btv`), folds it into the dedup hash, pushes `btv.*` keys, and exposes commands **`oans_arm_runway`** / **`oans_arm_exit`** (value=name) / **`oans_clear`** (plus `oans_display_airport` / `oans_set_manual_stop`). `FBWA380OansForm` builds a **BTV runway combo + "Arm runway"**, an **exit combo + "Arm exit"** (enabled once a runway is armed), and **"Clear BTV"** from the snapshot; the readout shows the armed runway (+ LDA), exit (+ distance), and dry/wet/stop predictions; and it **auto-announces on change** ("BTV armed, runway 22, exit E, 2835 metres" / "BTV cleared"). **Live-verified end-to-end at VCBI** (driving the agent directly): `snapshot().btv returns runways `["04","22"]`, after `armRunway("22")`+`armExit("E")` → `runway:"VCBI22", exit:"E", lda:3351, exitDist:2835`, exits `["A".."E"]`; `clearBtv()` resets to `runway:null`. (Source: `fbw-common/.../OANC/OansBrakeToVacateSelection.ts` + `Oanc.tsx`; selected idents live only on the event bus / observables, so the snapshot reads them from the ND JS instance, not SimVars.)

**OANS refinements (2026-06): units, ROT/turnaround, tab header, tab-aware search.**
- **Distance UNITS follow the metric toggle.** The OANS/BTV distances (LDA, exit distance, dry/wet/live-stop-bar) are stored in METRES but the real ND shows them in **M or FT per the metric setting** (FBW: `CONFIG_USING_METRIC_UNIT` → `UnitType.METER/FOOT`, factor 3.280839895). `snapshot().btv` reads **`A32NX_EFB_USING_METRIC_UNIT`** (the var MSFSBA already follows for weights, which tracks the EFB "US Units" toggle) as `metric`; the form's `Dist()` shows metres or feet accordingly. So OANS distances honour the same unit toggle as the rest of MSFSBA — verified `metric:true` live.
- **BTV ROT + TURNAROUND times (ARINC429-decoded).** `A32NX_BTV_ROT` (runway occupancy time, **seconds**) and `A32NX_BTV_TURNAROUND_{MAX,IDLE}_REVERSE` (brake-cooling time to next departure, **minutes**, idle = hotter brakes = longer) are **ARINC429** words. `coherent-oans-agent.js` `A._arinc(raw)` decodes them (low 32 bits = IEEE-754 float32 via `DataView`, SSM = bits 32-33; valid when SSM 3/2). Surfaced in the readout, **gated on an EXIT being armed** (matching the real OANS, which only shows them then). Live-verified the decode: `rot:30, turnMax:171, turnIdle:197` with an exit armed. Phrasing: "Runway occupancy time 30 seconds" / "Turnaround: 171 minutes max reverse, 197 minutes idle reverse".
- **Current-tab header + tab-aware search.** The readout drops the three tab lines (kept in the controls list to switch) and shows one **"Current tab: MAP DATA"** header derived from the `(active tab)` marker (live-verified clicking a tab moves the active marker). The **search box is tab-dependent** — the "Runway or exit" InputField on MAP DATA is the *airport-code* field on ARPT SEL (with ICAO/IATA/CITY radios) — so the form labels the search box from the live input's own label (`_searchField`, the text before the colon) and disables it when no input is present. `setValue` on the field is live-verified ("ok"); the taxiway search drives the FBW InputField (its accessible payoff is map-centering, so the future airport-diagram reader is the real "tell me about taxiway B" win).

**MFD navigation = click stable element id, NOT KCCU H-events.** FBW issue #9348 says the KCCU H-events are "practically unusable for external tools". The agent clicks the MFD page-selector menu item by its stable id `{CAPT|FO}_MFD_pageSelector{Tab}_{idx}` (the click fires even while the dropdown is collapsed); KCCU key is a cross-system fallback only. Current page is readable from SimVar `A380X_MFD_{L|R}_ACTIVE_PAGE` (string URI). All 20 pages are reachable from a **"Go to MFD page" combo** in `FBWA380MCDUForm` (`AllPages` table → `navigate_by_id`), the quick page buttons, or the MFD's own tabs. The scrape agent's `INTERACTIVE_SELECTOR`/`classify` also cover RadioButtonGroup (`.mfd-radio-button`, "(selected)"), in-page TopTabNavigator sub-tabs (`.mfd-top-tab-navigator-bar-element-outer`, "(active tab)" — e.g. PERF T.O/CLB/CRZ/DES/APPR/GA), SURV/ADS-C buttons, and context-menu items.
